			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Photovoltaic power station</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">  (Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_stations&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Photovoltaic power stations">Photovoltaic power stations</a>)</span></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Energiepark_Lauingen_Gehrlicher_Solar_AG.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Solar park" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Energiepark_Lauingen_Gehrlicher_Solar_AG.JPG/300px-Energiepark_Lauingen_Gehrlicher_Solar_AG.JPG" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Energiepark_Lauingen_Gehrlicher_Solar_AG.JPG/450px-Energiepark_Lauingen_Gehrlicher_Solar_AG.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Energiepark_Lauingen_Gehrlicher_Solar_AG.JPG/600px-Energiepark_Lauingen_Gehrlicher_Solar_AG.JPG 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Energiepark_Lauingen_Gehrlicher_Solar_AG.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 25.7 MW <a href="/wiki/Lauingen_Energy_Park" title="Lauingen Energy Park">Lauingen Energy Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Swabia" class="mw-redirect" title="Bavarian Swabia">Bavarian Swabia</a>, Germany</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A <b>photovoltaic power station</b>, also known as a <b>solar park</b>, is a large-scale <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic_system" title="Photovoltaic system">photovoltaic system</a> (PV system) designed for the supply of <a href="/wiki/Electricity_market#Wholesale_electricity_market" title="Electricity market">merchant power</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Electrical_grid" title="Electrical grid">electricity grid</a>. They are differentiated from most building-mounted and other decentralised solar power applications because they supply power at the <a href="/wiki/Utility" title="Utility">utility</a> level, rather than to a local user or users. They are sometimes also referred to as <b>solar farms</b> or <b>solar ranches</b>, especially when sited in agricultural areas. The generic expression <b>utility-scale solar</b> is sometimes used to describe this type of project.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a> source is via <a href="/wiki/Solar_panel" title="Solar panel">photovoltaic modules</a> that convert light directly to electricity. However, this differs from, and should not be confused with <a href="/wiki/Concentrated_solar_power" title="Concentrated solar power">concentrated solar power</a>, the other large-scale solar generation technology, which uses heat to drive a variety of conventional generator systems. Both approaches have their own advantages and disadvantages, but to date, for a variety of reasons, <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Photovoltaic">photovoltaic</a> technology has seen much wider use in the field. As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, PV systems outnumber concentrators by about 40 to 1.</p>
<p>In some countries, the <a href="/wiki/Nameplate_capacity" title="Nameplate capacity">nameplate capacity</a> of a photovoltaic power stations is rated in <a href="/wiki/Megawatt-peak" class="mw-redirect" title="Megawatt-peak">megawatt-peak</a> (MW<sub>p</sub>), which refers to the solar array's <a href="/wiki/Direct_current" title="Direct current">DC</a> power output. However, Canada, Japan, Spain and some parts of the United States often specify using the converted lower nominal power output in <a href="/wiki/Watt-peak_AC" class="mw-redirect" title="Watt-peak AC">MW<sub>AC</sub></a>; a measure directly comparable to other forms of power generation. A third and less common rating is the <a href="/wiki/Volt-ampere" title="Volt-ampere">mega volt-amperes</a> (MVA). Most solar parks are developed at a scale of at least 1&#160;MW<sub>p</sub>. As at the start of 2017, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_photovoltaic_power_stations" title="List of photovoltaic power stations">world's largest</a> operating photovoltaic power station has a capacity of over 800 <a href="/wiki/Megawatt" class="mw-redirect" title="Megawatt">megawatts</a> and projects up to 1 <a href="/wiki/Gigawatt" class="mw-redirect" title="Gigawatt">gigawatt</a> are planned. As at the end of 2016, about 4,300 projects with a combined capacity of 96&#160;GW<sub>AC</sub><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> were solar farms larger than 4&#160;MW<sub>AC</sub>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most of the existing large-scale photovoltaic power stations are owned and operated by independent power producers, but the involvement of community- and utility-owned projects is increasing. To date, almost all have been supported at least in part by regulatory incentives such as <a href="/wiki/Feed-in_tariff" title="Feed-in tariff">feed-in tariffs</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tax_credit#Renewable_Energy.2FInvestment_Tax_Credit_.28ITC.29" title="Tax credit">tax credits</a>, but as <a href="/wiki/Levelized_cost" class="mw-redirect" title="Levelized cost">levelized costs</a> have fallen significantly in the last decade and <a href="/wiki/Grid_parity" title="Grid parity">grid parity</a> has been reached in an increasing number of markets, it may not be long before external incentives cease to exist.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The first 1 MW<sub>p</sub> solar park was built by Arco Solar at Lugo near <a href="/wiki/Hesperia,_California" title="Hesperia, California">Hesperia, California</a> at the end of 1982,<sup id="cite_ref-Lugo_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lugo-4">[4]</a></sup> followed in 1984 by a 5.2 MW<sub>p</sub> installation in <a href="/wiki/Carrizo_Plain" title="Carrizo Plain">Carrizo Plain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Carrisa_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrisa-5">[5]</a></sup> Both have since been decommissioned, though Carrizo Plain is the site for several large plants now being constructed<sup id="cite_ref-Topaz_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Topaz-6">[6]</a></sup> or planned. The next stage followed the 2004 revisions<sup id="cite_ref-EEG2004_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EEG2004-7">[7]</a></sup> to the <a href="/wiki/Feed-in_tariffs_in_Germany" title="Feed-in tariffs in Germany">feed-in tariffs in Germany</a><sup id="cite_ref-solarplaza_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solarplaza-8">[8]</a></sup> when a substantial volume of solar parks were constructed.<sup id="cite_ref-solarplaza_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solarplaza-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SolarPowerPlantSerpa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/SolarPowerPlantSerpa.jpg/300px-SolarPowerPlantSerpa.jpg" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/SolarPowerPlantSerpa.jpg/450px-SolarPowerPlantSerpa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/SolarPowerPlantSerpa.jpg/600px-SolarPowerPlantSerpa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SolarPowerPlantSerpa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Serpa Solar Park built in Portugal in 2006</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Several hundred installations over 1 MW<sub>p</sub> have been since been installed in Germany, of which more than 50 are over 10 MW<sub>p</sub>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wiki-Germany_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wiki-Germany-9">[9]</a></sup> With its introduction of feed-in tariffs in 2008, Spain became briefly the largest market, with some 60 solar parks over 10 MW,<sup id="cite_ref-Spain_map_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spain_map-10">[10]</a></sup> but these incentives have since been withdrawn.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> The USA,<sup id="cite_ref-USA_map_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USA_map-12">[12]</a></sup> China<sup id="cite_ref-China_map_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China_map-13">[13]</a></sup> India,<sup id="cite_ref-India_map_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-India_map-14">[14]</a></sup> France,<sup id="cite_ref-France_map_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-France_map-15">[15]</a></sup> Canada,<sup id="cite_ref-Canada_map_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canada_map-16">[16]</a></sup> and Italy,<sup id="cite_ref-Italy_map_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Italy_map-17">[17]</a></sup> amongst others, have also become major markets as shown on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_photovoltaic_power_stations" title="List of photovoltaic power stations">list of photovoltaic power stations</a>.</p>
<p>The largest sites under construction have capacities of hundreds of MW<sub>p</sub> and projects at a scale of 1 GW<sub>p</sub> are being planned.<sup id="cite_ref-Topaz_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Topaz-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Siting_and_land_use">Siting and land use</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Siting and land use">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The land area required for a desired power output, varies depending on the location,<sup id="cite_ref-Statistics_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statistics-20">[20]</a></sup> and on the efficiency of the solar modules,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> the slope of the site<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> and the type of mounting used. Fixed tilt solar arrays using typical modules of about 15% efficiency<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> on horizontal sites, need about 1 <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">hectare</a>/MW in the tropics and this figure rises to over 2 <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">hectares</a> in northern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Statistics_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statistics-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>Because of the longer shadow the array casts when tilted at a steeper angle,<sup id="cite_ref-tilt_spacing_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tilt_spacing-24">[24]</a></sup> this area is typically about 10% higher for an adjustable tilt array or a single axis tracker, and 20% higher for a 2-axis tracker,<sup id="cite_ref-Wolfe_book_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolfe_book-25">[25]</a></sup> though these figures will vary depending on the latitude and topography.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>The best locations for solar parks in terms of land use are held to be brown field sites, or where there is no other valuable land use.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Even in cultivated areas, a significant proportion of the site of a solar farm can also be devoted to other productive uses, such as crop growing<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> or biodiversity.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agrivoltaics">Agrivoltaics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Agrivoltaics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Agrivoltaics" class="mw-redirect" title="Agrivoltaics">Agrivoltaics</a> is co-developing the same area of <a href="/wiki/Land" title="Land">land</a> for both solar <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Photovoltaic">photovoltaic</a> power as well as for conventional <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>. A recent study found that the value of solar generated electricity coupled to shade-tolerant crop production created an over 30% increase in economic value from farms deploying agrivoltaic systems instead of conventional agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Co-location">Co-location</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Co-location">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In some cases several different solar power stations, with separate owners and contractors, are developed on adjacent sites.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> This can offer the advantage of the projects sharing the cost and risks of project infrastructure such as grid connections and planning approval.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Solar farms can also be co-located with wind farms.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Sometimes the title 'solar park' is used, rather than an individual solar power station.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some examples of such solar clusters are the <a href="/wiki/Charanka_Solar_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Charanka Solar Park">Charanka Solar Park</a>, where there are 17 different generation projects; Neuhardenberg,<sup id="cite_ref-Neuhardenberg_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neuhardenberg-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> with eleven plants, and the Golmud solar parks with total reported capacity over 500MW.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Golmud_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Golmud-40">[40]</a></sup> An extreme example is calling all of the solar farms in the <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> state of India a single solar park, the <a href="/wiki/Gujarat_Solar_Park" title="Gujarat Solar Park">Gujarat Solar Park</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Most Solar parks are <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic_mounting_system#Ground_mounted" title="Photovoltaic mounting system">ground mounted</a> PV systems, also known as free-field solar power plants.<sup id="cite_ref-Free_field_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Free_field-41">[41]</a></sup> They can either be fixed tilt or use a single axis or dual axis <a href="/wiki/Solar_tracker" title="Solar tracker">solar tracker</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mounting_tilt_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mounting_tilt-42">[42]</a></sup> While tracking improves the overall performance, it also increases the system's installation and maintenance cost.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Solar_inverter" title="Solar inverter">solar inverter</a> converts the array's power output from <a href="/wiki/Direct_current" title="Direct current">DC</a> to <a href="/wiki/Alternating_current" title="Alternating current">AC</a>, and connection to the <a href="/wiki/Utility_grid" class="mw-redirect" title="Utility grid">utility grid</a> is made through a high voltage, three phase step up <a href="/wiki/Transformer" title="Transformer">transformer</a> of typically 10&#160;<a href="/wiki/Kilovolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Kilovolt">kV</a> and above.<sup id="cite_ref-transformer_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transformer-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Grid_voltage_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grid_voltage-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Solar_array_arrangements">Solar array arrangements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Solar array arrangements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Solar_array" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar array">solar arrays</a> are the subsystems which convert incoming light into electrical energy.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> They comprise a multitude of <a href="/wiki/Solar_module" class="mw-redirect" title="Solar module">solar modules</a>, mounted on support structures and interconnected to deliver a power output to electronic power conditioning subsystems.<sup id="cite_ref-system_schematic_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-system_schematic-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>A minority of utility-scale solar parks are configured on buildings<sup id="cite_ref-SolarServer_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SolarServer-49">[49]</a></sup> and so use <a href="/wiki/Bipv" class="mw-redirect" title="Bipv">building-mounted</a> solar arrays. The majority are 'free field' systems using ground-mounted structures,<sup id="cite_ref-Free_field_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Free_field-41">[41]</a></sup> usually of one of the following types:</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fixed_arrays">Fixed arrays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Fixed arrays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Many projects use mounting structures where the solar modules are mounted at a <a href="/wiki/Solar_tracker#Fixed_mount" title="Solar tracker">fixed</a> inclination calculated to provide the optimum annual output profile.<sup id="cite_ref-mounting_tilt_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mounting_tilt-42">[42]</a></sup> The modules are normally oriented towards the Equator, at a tilt angle slightly less than the latitude of the site.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> In some cases, depending on local climatic, topographical or electricity pricing regimes, different tilt angles can be used, or the arrays might be offset from the normal East-West axis to favour morning or evening output.<sup id="cite_ref-SEAI_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SEAI-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>A variant on this design is the use of arrays, whose tilt angle can be adjusted twice or four times annually to optimise seasonal output.<sup id="cite_ref-mounting_tilt_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mounting_tilt-42">[42]</a></sup> They also require more land area to reduce internal shading at the steeper winter tilt angle.<sup id="cite_ref-tilt_spacing_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tilt_spacing-24">[24]</a></sup> Because the increased output is typically only a few percent, it seldom justifies the increased cost and complexity of this design.<sup id="cite_ref-Wolfe_book_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolfe_book-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dual_axis_trackers">Dual axis trackers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Dual axis trackers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parc_fotovoltaic_de_Bellpuig_I.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Parc_fotovoltaic_de_Bellpuig_I.JPG/300px-Parc_fotovoltaic_de_Bellpuig_I.JPG" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Parc_fotovoltaic_de_Bellpuig_I.JPG/450px-Parc_fotovoltaic_de_Bellpuig_I.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Parc_fotovoltaic_de_Bellpuig_I.JPG/600px-Parc_fotovoltaic_de_Bellpuig_I.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parc_fotovoltaic_de_Bellpuig_I.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bellpuig Solar Park near <a href="/wiki/Lerida" class="mw-redirect" title="Lerida">Lerida, Spain</a> uses pole-mounted 2-axis trackers</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To maximise the intensity of incoming direct radiation, solar panels should be orientated normal to the sun's rays.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> To achieve this, arrays can be designed using <a href="/wiki/Solar_tracker#Dual_axis_trackers" title="Solar tracker">two-axis trackers</a>, capable of tracking the sun in its daily orbit across the sky, and as its elevation changes throughout the year.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>These arrays need to be spaced out to reduce inter-shading as the sun moves and the array orientations change, so need more land area.<sup id="cite_ref-Trackers_REW_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trackers_REW-54">[54]</a></sup> They also require more complex mechanisms to maintain the array surface at the required angle. The increased output can be of the order of 30%<sup id="cite_ref-Trackers_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trackers-55">[55]</a></sup> in locations with high levels of <a href="/wiki/Direct_insolation" title="Direct insolation">direct radiation</a>, but the increase is lower in temperate climates or those with more significant <a href="/wiki/Diffuse_sky_radiation" title="Diffuse sky radiation">diffuse radiation</a>, due to overcast conditions. For this reason, dual axis trackers are most commonly used in subtropical regions,<sup id="cite_ref-Trackers_REW_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trackers_REW-54">[54]</a></sup> and were first deployed at utility scale at the Lugo plant.<sup id="cite_ref-Lugo_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lugo-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Single_axis_trackers">Single axis trackers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Single axis trackers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A third approach achieves some of the output benefits of tracking, with a lesser penalty in terms of land area, capital and operating cost. This involves tracking the sun in one dimension – in its daily journey across the sky – but not adjusting for the seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-NREL_tracker_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NREL_tracker-56">[56]</a></sup> The angle of the axis is normally horizontal, though some, such as the solar park at Nellis Airforce Base, which have a 20° tilt,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> incline the axis towards the equator in a north-south orientation – effectively a hybrid between tracking and fixed tilt.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Solar_tracker#Single_axis_trackers" title="Solar tracker">Single axis tracking systems</a> are aligned along axes roughly North-South.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Some use linkages between rows so that the same actuator can adjust the angle of several rows at once.<sup id="cite_ref-NREL_tracker_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NREL_tracker-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Power_conversion">Power conversion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Power conversion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Solar panels produce <a href="/wiki/Direct_current" title="Direct current">direct current</a> (DC) electricity, so solar parks need conversion equipment<sup id="cite_ref-system_schematic_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-system_schematic-48">[48]</a></sup> to convert this to <a href="/wiki/Alternating_current" title="Alternating current">alternating current</a> (AC), which is the form transmitted by the electricity grid. This conversion is done by <a href="/wiki/Inverter" class="mw-redirect" title="Inverter">inverters</a>. To maximise their efficiency, solar power plants also incorporate <a href="/wiki/Maximum_power_point_trackers" class="mw-redirect" title="Maximum power point trackers">maximum power point trackers</a>, either within the inverters or as separate units. These devices keep each solar array string close to its <a href="/wiki/Solar_cell_efficiency#Maximum_power_point" title="Solar cell efficiency">peak power point</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are two primary alternatives for configuring this conversion equipment; centralised and string inverters,<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> although in some cases individual, or <a href="/wiki/Solar_micro-inverter" title="Solar micro-inverter">micro-inverters</a> are used.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Single inverters allows optimizing the output of each panel, and multiple inverters increases the reliability by limiting the loss of output when an inverter fails.<sup id="cite_ref-casestudy_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-casestudy-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Centralised_inverters">Centralised inverters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Centralised inverters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Juwi_PV_Field.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Juwi_PV_Field.jpg/300px-Juwi_PV_Field.jpg" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Juwi_PV_Field.jpg/450px-Juwi_PV_Field.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Juwi_PV_Field.jpg/600px-Juwi_PV_Field.jpg 2x" data-file-width="673" data-file-height="449" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Juwi_PV_Field.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Waldpolenz_Solar_Park" title="Waldpolenz Solar Park">Waldpolenz Solar Park</a><sup id="cite_ref-Waldpolenz_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Waldpolenz-64">[64]</a></sup> is divided into blocks, each with a centralised inverter</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>These units have relatively high capacity, typically of the order of 1 MW,<sup id="cite_ref-inverters_REW_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inverters_REW-65">[65]</a></sup> so they condition that the output of a substantial block of solar arrays, up to perhaps 2 hectares (4.9 acres) in area.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Solar parks using centralised inverters are often configured in discrete rectangular blocks, with the related inverter in one corner, or the centre of the block.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="String_inverters">String inverters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: String inverters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/String_inverter" class="mw-redirect" title="String inverter">String inverters</a> are substantially lower in capacity, of the order of 10&#160;kW,<sup id="cite_ref-inverters_REW_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inverters_REW-65">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> and condition the output of a single array string. This is normally a whole, or part of, a row of solar arrays within the overall plant. String inverters can enhance the efficiency of solar parks, where different parts of the array are experiencing different levels of insolation, for example where arranged at different orientations, or closely packed to minimise site area.<sup id="cite_ref-casestudy_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-casestudy-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Transformers">Transformers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Transformers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The system inverters typically provide power output at voltages of the order of 480 V<sub>AC</sub>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-planning_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-planning-72">[72]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Electrical_grid" title="Electrical grid">Electricity grids</a> operate at much higher voltages of the order of tens or hundreds of thousands of volts,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> so transformers are incorporated to deliver the required output to the grid.<sup id="cite_ref-Grid_voltage_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grid_voltage-46">[46]</a></sup> Due to the long lead time, the <a href="/wiki/Long_Island_Solar_Farm" title="Long Island Solar Farm">Long Island Solar Farm</a> chose to keep a spare transformer onsite, as transformer failure would have kept the solar farm offline for a long period.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Transformers typically have a life of 25 to 75 years, and normally do not require replacement during the life of a photovoltaic power station.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="System_performance">System performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: System performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The performance of a solar park is a function of the climatic conditions, the equipment used and the system configuration. The primary energy input is the global light irradiance in the plane of the solar arrays, and this in turn is a combination of the direct and the diffuse radiation.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>A key determinant of the output of the system is the conversion efficiency of the solar modules, which will depend in particular on the type of <a href="/wiki/Solar_cell" title="Solar cell">solar cell</a> used.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>There will be losses between the DC output of the solar modules and the AC power delivered to the grid, due to a wide range of factors such as light absorption losses, mismatch, cable voltage drop, conversion efficiencies, and other parasitic losses.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> A parameter called the 'performance ratio'<sup id="cite_ref-PerfRatio_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PerfRatio-79">[79]</a></sup> has been developed to evaluate the total value of these losses. The performance ratio gives a measure of the output AC power delivered as a proportion of the total DC power which the solar modules should be able to deliver under the ambient climatic conditions. In modern solar parks the performance ratio should typically be in excess of 80%.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="System_degradation">System degradation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: System degradation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Early photovoltaic systems output decreased as much as 10%/year,<sup id="cite_ref-Carrisa_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Carrisa-5">[5]</a></sup> but as of 2010 the median degradation rate was 0.5%/year, with modules made after 2000 having a significantly lower degradation rate, so that a system would lose only 12% of its output performance in 25 years. A system using modules which degrade 4%/year will lose 64% of its output during the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> Many panel makers offer a performance guarantee, typically 90% in ten years and 80% over 25 years. The output of all panels is typically warranteed at plus or minus 3% during the first year of operation.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_business_of_developing_solar_parks">The business of developing solar parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: The business of developing solar parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Westmill_Solar_Cooperative_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Westmill_Solar_Cooperative_1.jpg/300px-Westmill_Solar_Cooperative_1.jpg" width="300" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Westmill_Solar_Cooperative_1.jpg/450px-Westmill_Solar_Cooperative_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Westmill_Solar_Cooperative_1.jpg/600px-Westmill_Solar_Cooperative_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1987" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Westmill_Solar_Cooperative_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Westmill_Solar_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Westmill Solar Park">Westmill Solar Park</a><sup id="cite_ref-WSC_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSC-84">[84]</a></sup> is the world's largest community-owned solar power station<sup id="cite_ref-Westmill_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Westmill-85">[85]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Solar power plants are developed to deliver merchant electricity into the grid as an alternative to other renewable, fossil or nuclear generating stations.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>The plant owner is an electricity generator. Most solar power plants today are owned by <a href="/wiki/Independent_power_producer" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent power producer">independent power producers</a> (IPP's),<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> though some are held by <a href="/wiki/Investor-owned_utility" title="Investor-owned utility">investor-</a> or <a href="/wiki/Utility_cooperative" title="Utility cooperative">community-owned</a> utilities.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some of these power producers develop their own portfolio of power plants,<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> but most solar parks are initially designed and constructed by specialist project developers.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Typically the developer will plan the project, obtain planning and connection consents, and arrange financing for the capital required.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> The actual construction work is normally contracted to one or more <a href="/w/index.php?title=EPC_(contract)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="EPC (contract) (page does not exist)">EPC</a> (engineering, procurement and construction) contractors.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>Major milestones in the development of a new photovoltaic power plant are planning consent,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> grid connection approval,<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> financial close,<sup id="cite_ref-SunEdison_SA_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SunEdison_SA-95">[95]</a></sup> construction,<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> connection and commissioning.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> At each stage in the process, the developer will be able to update estimates of the anticipated performance and costs of the plant and the financial returns it should be able to deliver.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Planning_approval">Planning approval</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Planning approval">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Photovoltaic power stations occupy at least one <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">hectare</a> for each megawatt of rated output,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> so require a substantial land area; which is subject to planning approval. The chances of obtaining consent, and the related time, cost and conditions, varying from jurisdiction to jurisdiction and location to location. Many planning approvals will also apply conditions on the treatment of the site after the station has been decommissioned in the future.<sup id="cite_ref-planning_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-planning-72">[72]</a></sup> A professional health, safety and environment assessment is usually undertaken during the design of a PV power station in order to ensure the facility is designed and planned in accordance with all <a href="/wiki/Health,_Safety_and_Environment" class="mw-redirect" title="Health, Safety and Environment">HSE</a> regulations.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grid_connection">Grid connection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Grid connection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The availability, locality and capacity of the connection to the grid is a major consideration in planning a new solar park, and can be a significant contributor to the cost.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<p>Most stations are sited within a few kilometres of a suitable grid connection point. This network needs to be capable of absorbing the output of the solar park when operating at its maximum capacity. The project developer will normally have to absorb the cost of providing power lines to this point and making the connection; in addition often to any costs associated with upgrading the grid, so it can accommodate the output from the plant.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operation_and_maintenance">Operation and maintenance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Operation and maintenance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Once the solar park has been commissioned, the owner usually enters into a contract with a suitable counterparty to undertake operation and maintenance (O&amp;M).<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> In many cases this may be fulfilled by the original EPC contractor.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>Solar plants' reliable solid-state systems require minimal maintenance, compared to rotating machinery for example.<sup id="cite_ref-low_maintenance_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-low_maintenance-104">[104]</a></sup> A major aspect of the O&amp;M contract will be continuous monitoring of the performance of the plant and all of its primary subsystems,<sup id="cite_ref-OandM_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OandM-105">[105]</a></sup> which is normally undertaken remotely.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> This enables performance to be compared with the anticipated output under the climatic conditions actually experienced.<sup id="cite_ref-SunEdison_SA_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SunEdison_SA-95">[95]</a></sup> It also provides data to enable the scheduling of both rectification and preventive maintenance.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> A small number of large solar farms use a separate inverter<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> or maximizer<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> for each solar panel, which provide individual performance data that can be monitored. For other solar farms, thermal imaging is a tool that is used to identify non-performing panels for replacement.<sup id="cite_ref-pv2012_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pv2012-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Power_delivery">Power delivery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Power delivery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A solar park's income derives from the sales of electricity to the grid, and so its output is metered in real-time with readings of its energy output provided, typically on a half-hourly basis, for balancing and settlement within the electricity market.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>Income is affected by the reliability of equipment within the plant and also by the availability of the grid network to which it is exporting.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Some connection contracts allow the <a href="/wiki/Transmission_system_operator" title="Transmission system operator">transmission system operator</a> to constrain the output of a solar park, for example at times of low demand or high availability of other generators.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Some countries make statutory provision for priority access to the grid<sup id="cite_ref-Priority_access_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Priority_access-115">[115]</a></sup> for renewable generators, such as that under the European <a href="/wiki/Renewables_Directive" class="mw-redirect" title="Renewables Directive">Renewable Energy Directive</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economics_and_Finance">Economics and Finance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Economics and Finance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In recent years, PV technology has improved its electricity generating <a href="/wiki/Solar_cell_efficiency" title="Solar cell efficiency">efficiency</a>, reduced the installation <a href="/wiki/Price_per_watt" title="Price per watt">cost per watt</a> as well as its <a href="/wiki/Energy_payback_time" class="mw-redirect" title="Energy payback time">energy payback time</a> (EPBT), and has reached <a href="/wiki/Grid_parity" title="Grid parity">grid parity</a> in at least 19 different markets by 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Photovoltaics is increasingly becoming a viable source of mainstream power.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> However, prices for PV systems show strong regional variations, much more than solar cells and panels, which tend to be global commodities. In 2013, utility-scale system prices in highly penetrated markets such as China and Germany were significantly lower ($1.40/W) than in the United States ($3.30/W). The <a href="/wiki/International_Energy_Agency" title="International Energy Agency">IEA</a> explains these discrepancies due to differences in "soft costs", which include customer acquisition, permitting, inspection and interconnection, installation labor and financing costs.<sup id="cite_ref-IEA-roadmap-PV-2014_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IEA-roadmap-PV-2014-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:14</sup></p>
<table class="wikitable sortable floatright" style="text-align: center; width: 240px;">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grid_parity">Grid parity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Grid parity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Grid_parity" title="Grid parity">Grid parity</a></div>
<p>Solar generating stations have become progressively cheaper in recent years, and this trend is expected to continue.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> Meanwhile, traditional electricity generation is becoming progressively more expensive.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> These trends are expected to lead to a crossover point when the levelised cost of energy from solar parks, historically more expensive, matches the cost of traditional electricity generation.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> This point is commonly referred to as grid parity.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>For merchant solar power stations, where the electricity is being sold into the electricity transmission network, the levelised cost of solar energy will need to match the wholesale electricity price. This point is sometimes called 'wholesale grid parity' or 'busbar parity'.<sup id="cite_ref-UN-Energy-2012_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN-Energy-2012-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some photovoltaic systems, such as rooftop installations, can supply power directly to an electricity user. In these cases, the installation can be competitive when the output cost matches the price at which the user pays for his electricity consumption. This situation is sometimes called 'retail grid parity', 'socket parity' or 'dynamic grid parity'.<sup id="cite_ref-EPIA_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EPIA-126">[126]</a></sup> Research carried out by <a href="/wiki/UN-Energy" title="UN-Energy">UN-Energy</a> in 2012 suggests areas of sunny countries with high electricity prices, such as Italy, Spain and Australia, and areas using diesel generators, have reached retail grid parity.<sup id="cite_ref-UN-Energy-2012_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN-Energy-2012-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Incentive_mechanisms">Incentive mechanisms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Incentive mechanisms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Because the point of grid parity has not yet been reached in many parts of the world, solar generating stations need some form of financial incentive to compete for the supply of electricity.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Many legislatures around the world have introduced such incentives to support the deployment of solar power stations.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Feed-in_tariffs">Feed-in tariffs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Feed-in tariffs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Feed-in_tariff" title="Feed-in tariff">Feed-in tariff</a></div>
<p>Feed in tariffs are designated prices which must be paid by utility companies for each kilowatt hour of renewable electricity produced by qualifying generators and fed into the grid.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> These tariffs normally represent a premium on wholesale electricity prices and offer a guaranteed revenue stream to help the power producer finance the project.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Renewable_portfolio_standards_and_supplier_obligations">Renewable portfolio standards and supplier obligations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Renewable portfolio standards and supplier obligations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Renewable_portfolio_standard" title="Renewable portfolio standard">Renewable portfolio standard</a></div>
<p>These standards are obligations on utility companies to source a proportion of their electricity from renewable generators.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> In most cases, they do not prescribe which technology should be used and the utility is free to select the most appropriate renewable sources.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are some exceptions where solar technologies are allocated a proportion of the RPS in what is sometimes referred to as a 'solar set aside'.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Loan_guarantees_and_other_capital_incentives">Loan guarantees and other capital incentives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Loan guarantees and other capital incentives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Loan_guarantee" title="Loan guarantee">Loan guarantee</a></div>
<p>Some countries and states adopt less targeted financial incentives, available for a wide range of infrastructure investment, such as the US Department of Energy loan guarantee scheme,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> which stimulated a number of investments in the solar power plant in 2010 and 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tax_credits_and_other_fiscal_incentives">Tax credits and other fiscal incentives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Tax credits and other fiscal incentives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tax_credit" title="Tax credit">Tax credit</a></div>
<p>Another form of indirect incentive which has been used to stimulate investment in solar power plant was tax credits available to investors. In some cases the credits were linked to the energy produced by the installations, such as the Production Tax Credits.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> In other cases the credits were related to the capital investment such as the Investment Tax Credits<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="International.2C_national_and_regional_programmes">International, national and regional programmes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: International, national and regional programmes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In addition to free market commercial incentives, some countries and regions have specific programs to support the deployment of solar energy installations.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Renewables_Directive" class="mw-redirect" title="Renewables Directive">Renewables Directive</a><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> sets targets for increasing levels of deployment of renewable energy in all member states. Each has been required to develop a <a href="/wiki/National_Renewable_Energy_Action_Plan" title="National Renewable Energy Action Plan">National Renewable Energy Action Plan</a> showing how these targets would be met, and many of these have specific support measures for solar energy deployment.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> The directive also allows states to develop projects outside their national boundaries, and this may lead to bilateral programs such as the Helios project.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Clean_Development_Mechanism" title="Clean Development Mechanism">Clean Development Mechanism</a><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> of the <a href="/wiki/UNFCCC" class="mw-redirect" title="UNFCCC">UNFCCC</a> is an international programme under which solar generating stations in certain qualifying countries can be supported.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>Additionally many other countries have specific solar energy development programmes. Some examples are <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru_National_Solar_Mission" title="Jawaharlal Nehru National Solar Mission">JNNSM</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> the Flagship Program in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> and similar projects in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_performance">Financial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Financial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The financial performance of the solar power plant is a function of its income and its costs.<sup id="cite_ref-Wolfe_book_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolfe_book-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>The electrical output of a solar park will be related to the solar radiation, the capacity of the plant and its performance ratio.<sup id="cite_ref-PerfRatio_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PerfRatio-79">[79]</a></sup> The income derived from this electrical output will come primarily from the sale of the electricity,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> and any incentive payments such as those under Feed-in Tariffs or other support mechanisms.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p>Electricity prices may vary at different times of day, giving a higher price at times of high demand.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> This may influence the design of the plant to increase its output at such times.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>The dominant costs of solar power plants are the capital cost, and therefore any associated financing and depreciation.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> Though operating costs are typically relatively low, especially as no fuel is required,<sup id="cite_ref-low_maintenance_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-low_maintenance-104">[104]</a></sup> most operators will want to ensure that adequate operation and maintenance cover<sup id="cite_ref-OandM_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OandM-105">[105]</a></sup> is available to maximise the availability of the plant and thereby optimise the income to cost ratio.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_by_country" title="Solar power by country">Solar power by country</a> and <a href="/wiki/Growth_of_photovoltaics" title="Growth of photovoltaics">Growth of photovoltaics</a></div>
<p>The first places to reach grid parity were those with high traditional electricity prices and high levels of solar radiation.<sup id="cite_ref-Statistics_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statistics-20">[20]</a></sup> Currently, more capacity is being installed in the <a href="/wiki/Rooftop_photovoltaic_power_station" title="Rooftop photovoltaic power station">rooftop</a> than in the utility-scale segment. However, the worldwide distribution of solar parks is expected to change as different regions achieve grid parity.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> This transition also includes a shift from rooftop towards utility-scale plants, since the focus of new PV deployment has changed from Europe towards the <i>Sunbelt markets</i> where ground-mounted PV systems are favored.<sup id="cite_ref-epia-2014_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-epia-2014-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:43</sup></p>
<p>Because of the economic background, large-scale systems are presently distributed where the support regimes have been the most consistent, or the most advantageous.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Total capacity of worldwide PV plants above 4 MW<sub>AC</sub> was assessed by <a href="/wiki/Wiki-Solar" title="Wiki-Solar">Wiki-Solar</a> as 36 GW in c. 2,300 installations at the end of 2014<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> and represents about 25 percent of total global PV capacity of 139&#160;GW.<sup id="cite_ref-epia-2014_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-epia-2014-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:17</sup> The countries which had the most capacity, in descending order, were the <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_the_United_States" title="Solar power in the United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_China" title="Solar power in China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_Germany" title="Solar power in Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_India" title="Solar power in India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Solar power in the United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_Spain" title="Solar power in Spain">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_Italy" title="Solar power in Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_Canada" title="Solar power in Canada">Canada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_South_Africa" title="Solar power in South Africa">South Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> Activities in the key markets are reviewed individually below.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_China" title="Solar power in China">Solar power in China</a></div>
<p>China was reported in early 2013 to have overtaken Germany as the nation with the most utility-scale solar capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-Capacity_2013_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Capacity_2013-158">[158]</a></sup> Much of this has been supported by the <a href="/wiki/Clean_Development_Mechanism" title="Clean Development Mechanism">Clean Development Mechanism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> The distribution of power plants around the country is quite broad, with the highest concentration in the Gobi desert<sup id="cite_ref-China_map_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China_map-13">[13]</a></sup> and connected to the Northwest China Power Grid.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_Germany" title="Solar power in Germany">Solar power in Germany</a></div>
<p>The first multi-megawatt plant in Europe was the 4.2 MW community-owned project at Hemau, commissioned in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-Hemau_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hemau-161">[161]</a></sup> But it was the revisions to the German feed-in tariffs in 2004,<sup id="cite_ref-EEG2004_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EEG2004-7">[7]</a></sup> which gave the strongest impetus to the establishment of utility-scale solar power plants.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> The first to be completed under this programme was the Leipziger Land solar park developed by Geosol.<sup id="cite_ref-Leipziger_Land_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leipziger_Land-163">[163]</a></sup> Several dozen plants were built between 2004 and 2011, several of which were at the time the <a href="#Noteworthy_solar_parks">largest in the world</a>. The <a href="/wiki/German_Renewable_Energy_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="German Renewable Energy Act">EEG</a>, the law which establishes Germany’s feed-in tariffs, provides the legislative basis not just for the compensation levels, but other regulatory factors, such as priority access to the grid.<sup id="cite_ref-Priority_access_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Priority_access-115">[115]</a></sup> The law was amended in 2010 to restrict the use of agricultural land,<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> since which time most solar parks have been built on so-called ‘development land’, such as former military sites.<sup id="cite_ref-Neuhardenberg_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neuhardenberg-37">[37]</a></sup> Partly for this reason, the geographic distribution of photovoltaic power plants in Germany<sup id="cite_ref-Wiki-Germany_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wiki-Germany-9">[9]</a></sup> is biased towards the former Eastern Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> As of February 2012, Germany had 1.1 million photovoltaic power plants (most are small kW roof mounted).<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_India" title="Solar power in India">Solar power in India</a></div>
<p>India has been rising up the leading nations for the installation of utility-scale solar capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-Capacity_2013_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Capacity_2013-158">[158]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Charanka_Solar_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Charanka Solar Park">Charanka Solar Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> was opened officially in April 2012<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> and was at the time the <a href="#Noteworthy_solar_parks">largest group of solar power plants</a> in the world. Geographically the majority of the stations are located in <a href="/wiki/Gujarat" title="Gujarat">Gujarat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maharashtra" title="Maharashtra">Maharashtra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-India_map_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-India_map-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rajasthan" title="Rajasthan">Rajasthan</a> has successfully been attempting to attract solar development.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> Rajasthan and Gujarat share the <a href="/wiki/Thar_Desert" title="Thar Desert">Thar Desert</a>, along with Pakistan.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_Italy" title="Solar power in Italy">Solar power in Italy</a></div>
<p>Italy has a very large number of photovoltaic power plants, the largest of which is the 84 MW <a href="/wiki/Montalto_di_Castro_Photovoltaic_Power_Station" title="Montalto di Castro Photovoltaic Power Station">Montalto di Castro project</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_Spain" title="Solar power in Spain">Solar power in Spain</a></div>
<p>The majority of the deployment of solar power stations in Spain to date occurred during the boom market of 2007-8.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> The stations are well distributed around the country, with some concentration in <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">Extremadura</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castile-La_Mancha" class="mw-redirect" title="Castile-La Mancha">Castile-La Mancha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Murcia" title="Murcia">Murcia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Spain_map_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spain_map-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Solar power in the United Kingdom">Solar power in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<p>The introduction of <a href="/wiki/Feed-in_tariffs_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Feed-in tariffs in the United Kingdom">Feed-in tariffs in the United Kingdom</a> in 2010 stimulated the first wave of utility-scale projects,<sup id="cite_ref-WolfeWare_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WolfeWare-172">[172]</a></sup> with c. 20 plants being completed<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> before tariffs were reduced on 1 August 2011 following the 'Fast Track Review'.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> A second wave of installations was undertaken under the UK's <a href="/wiki/Renewables_Obligation" class="mw-redirect" title="Renewables Obligation">Renewables Obligation</a>, with the total number of plants connected by the end of March 2013 reaching 86.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> This is reported to have made the UK Europe's best market in the first quarter of 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<p>UK projects were originally concentrated in the South West, but have more recently spread across the South of England and into East Anglia and the Midlands.<sup id="cite_ref-UK_map_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UK_map-177">[177]</a></sup> The first solar park in Wales came on stream in 2011 at <a href="/wiki/Rhoshill,_Pembrokeshire" title="Rhoshill, Pembrokeshire">Rhosygilwen</a>, north <a href="/wiki/Pembrokeshire" title="Pembrokeshire">Pembrokeshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> As of June 2014 there were 18 schemes generating more than 5&#160;MW and 34 in planning or construction in Wales.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_the_United_States" title="Solar power in the United States">Solar power in the United States</a></div>
<p>The US deployment of photovoltaic power stations is largely concentrated in southwestern states.<sup id="cite_ref-USA_map_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USA_map-12">[12]</a></sup> The Renewable Portfolio Standards in California<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> and surrounding states<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> provide a particular incentive. The volume of projects under construction in early 2013 has led to the forecast that the US will become the leading market.<sup id="cite_ref-Capacity_2013_158-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Capacity_2013-158">[158]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noteworthy_solar_parks">Noteworthy solar parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Photovoltaic_power_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Noteworthy solar parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_photovoltaic_power_stations" title="List of photovoltaic power stations">List of photovoltaic power stations</a></div>
